SEMESTER S5 
MARITIME LAW AND SHIPPING MANAGEMENT 
Course Code 
PENST525 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T: P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCNST205 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the role of international conventions in formulating Maritime Law, the roles of 
Maritime Labour Convention and international conventions on the Law of the Sea. 
2. Understand the roles of international conventions for the Safety of Life at Sea, International 
Ship and Port Facility Security Code (ISPS Code), and other conventions 
3. To enable the student to understand the basic structure of shipping industry and the role of 
various stakeholders in the industry 
4. To provide the student an understanding of shipping economics and the shipping market 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to maritime law; need and source of maritime law; 
implementation of maritime law through national legislation; role of United 
Nations (UN), International Maritime Organization (IMO) and International 
Labour Organization (ILO); role of Flag state and Port state in 
implementation of law; introduction to SOLAS, MARPOL, STCW and 
Maritime Labour Convention (MLC); need of survey and certification. 
Classification Societies, need and role of Classification Societies. United 
Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea (UNCLOS), various zones and 
limits. 
Maritime Labour Convention, minimum requirements for seafarers to work 
on a ship, conditions of employment, accommodation, recreational facilities, 
food and catering, health protection, medical care, welfare and social 
security. 
11 

 
 
2 
SOLAS- Introduction to SOLAS; Subdivision and stability; Fire protection, 
detection and extinction; Lifesaving appliances and arrangements; Carriage 
of grain; Carriage of dangerous goods.  
Load Line Convention, important definitions and markings, survey and 
certification. 
ISPS Code, ship security plan, security levels, declaration of security, ship 
security alert system, piracy, best management practices to deter piracy. 
Introduction to other Conventions; International Convention on Salvage, 
Convention on Limitation of Liability for Maritime Claims, Oil Pollution 
Compensation Conventions. 
11 
3 
Shipping Management- Types of cargoes, types of ships which carry them; 
Ship’s tonnages (GT, NT); Cargo carrying capacity. Ship registration, ship 
insurance. Ship owners, operators and managers. Types of shipping services- 
liner and tramp. Role of intermediaries in shipping business- freight brokers, 
clearing and forwarding agents, stevedores, shipbrokers, bunker and stores 
suppliers, shipping agencies. 
11 
4 
Shipping Economics-Sea transport and the global economy, role of shipping 
in economic development. Shipping market cycles, shipping risk, shipping 
market supply and demand model. The four shipping markets- freight 
market, sale and purchase market, newbuilding market and demolition 
market.  Classification of costs, Financing ships and shipping companies, 
Risk and returns. 
11 
 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly defines the legal or shipping management  problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, 
objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and present a well-reasoned solution approach based on legal 
or management perspectives. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with technical evidence. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compare trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Consider feasibility and practical implications. 
4. Design Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions. 
b. Successfully translate the chosen solution into tangible outputs. 
 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate 
for the problem. (K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 
understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 

 
 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S5 
MARINE HYDRODYNAMICS AND HYDRAULICS LAB 
Course Code 
PCNSL507 
CIE Marks 
50 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T: P: R) 
0:0:3:0 
ESE Marks  
50 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCNST205 
PBNST304 
PCNST402  
Course Type 
Lab 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Apply knowledge in marine hydrodynamics and hydraulic machinery experimentally. 
2. Understand the arrangement and conduct of experiments in the Marine Hydrodynamics & 
Hydraulic Machinery laboratory. 
3. Comprehend the factors responsible for variation between theoretical and experimental 
results pertaining to the domain of Marine Hydrodynamics & Hydraulic Machinery. 
4. Able to note down relevant readings and perform calculations while an experiment is in 
progress thereby correlating theoretical concepts of marine hydrodynamics and their practical 
implications on ship. 
 
Expt.  
No. 
Experiments (Minimum 12 are mandatory) 
1 
Performance Characteristic Tests on Pelton Wheel (Load test & best speed). - Equipment: 
Pelton Wheel Turbine Test Rig. 
2 
Performance Characteristic Tests on Francis Turbine (Load test & best gate opening). - 
Equipment: Francis Turbine Test Rig. 
3 
Performance Characteristic Tests on Kaplan Turbine (Load test & best gate, vane angle 
opening) - Equipment: Kaplan Turbine Test Rig. 
4 
Performance characteristic Tests on Single Stage, Multi Stage Centrifugal Pumps at 
Constant Speed & at Variable Speed. (Actual & predicted curves) - Equipment:

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test understanding of 
the upcoming experiment. 
 Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of the 
theoretical background related to the experiments. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of experiments, 
and following safety protocols. 
 Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper documentation of 
experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
 
 

 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles 
during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, and 
record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and understanding 
each step involved. 
 Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing materials/equipment. 
 Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the experiment. 
 Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or programming 
task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality of 
program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the subject. 
 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 
Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted  

 
 
SEMESTER S5 
SHIP DESIGN LAB 
Course Code

Course Type 
Lab 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the methodologies for modelling 3D bodies like ships and submarines 
2. Generate faired lines plan for given offset table. 
3. Generate hydrostatics particulars and Bonjean data and get the plots of the curves. 
4. Analyse stability (intact and damaged) parameters of the ship using the generated model 
 
Expt.  
No. 
Experiments (Minimum 12 are mandatory) 
1 
Study various approaches in generating lines plan of ships. 
2 
Modelling of hull surface from offset data. 
3 
Modelling of hull surface by modifying general hull form from software database. 
4 
Solid modelling from boundary surfaces (e.g. superstructure). 
5 
Solid modelling by revolving closed areas about an axis (e.g. Submarine hull). 
6 
Bow thruster tunnel modelling. 
7 
Modelling of tanks and cargo spaces. 
8 
Plotting lines plan of a vessel from given offset table. 
9 
Computation and plotting of Bonjean and sectional area curve. 
10 
Computation of ship hydrostatic particulars. 
11 
Calculate equilibrium condition of a given ship at given loading conditions. 
12 
Computation of transverse metacentric height. 
13 
Computation of stability at small and large angles of heel.

SEMESTER S6 
 
NAVAL ARCHITECTURE & SHIPBUILDING 
ENGINEERING 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
 
 
 
SEMESTER S6 
SHIP STRUCTURES II 
Course Code 
PCNST601 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-1-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCNST502 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the loads acting on the hull girder, modes of failure and hull girder global 
response 
2. Understand the response of hull girder to wave loads,  
3. Understand the effect of torsion and buckling on hull girder strength and the concept of limit 
state analysis. 
4. Understand the basics of vibration and fatigue as applicable to marine structures. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Loads and moments acting on ship structures in still water and in waves, 
modes of failure in sagging, hogging and torsion, weight and weight 
distribution, buoyancy and buoyancy distribution, load curve, shear force 
curve, bending moment curve, deflection curve, effect of thermal loads. 
 
11  
2 
Loads imposed by regular waves and oblique waves, representation of 
irregular seaway, short term and long term distribution of loads, spectral 
approach to response of ship structures, effect of slamming and shipping of 
green seas. 
 
11  
3 
Torsional loads due to oblique waves and cargo distribution, torsion 
warping deformations and stresses, torsion of container ships, shear stress 
distribution procedure, limit states - ultimate, serviceability, fatigue, 
11 

 
 
accidental limit states, ultimate strength assessment of hull girder using 
progressive collapse analysis. 
4 
Classification of vibration, introduction to hull structure vibration, modes of 
hull structure vibration, sources of vibration, measures for control of 
vibration, fatigue failures of marine structures, Main Contributing Factors 
to Fatigue, Fatigue Design Strategies 
 
11

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1.  Understand the basics features of offshore structures 
2. Discern the basic principles of fixed offshore platform design 
3. Discern the basic principles of Compliant offshore structures design 
4. Understand the basics of offshore installation. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Definition and functions of Offshore structures, Brief Historical 
Development, Different types of Offshore Structure Configurations: Bottom 
Supported Fixed Structures, Compliant Structures, Floating Structures and 
Novel & Small Field Offshore Structures, Offshore field development 
concepts and design phases 
9  
2 
Waves and wave theories, Wave force on offshore structures: Small diameter 
and large diameter structures, vertical and arbitrarily oriented cylindrical 
members, Ocean currents and current forces exerted on offshore structures, 
Wind forces, Earthquake forces, Ice forces and Tides, Marine growth, 
Response of offshore structures to ocean environment, Introduction to 
corrosion and protection of offshore structures 
9  
3 
Design spiral, Various types of loads acting on offshore structures, 
Introduction to design tools for offshore structure design, Jacket structure: 
Basic configuration, sizing considerations, design strategy, bracing system, 
jacket design, pile design, deck design, top sides, appurtenances, Floating 
Structures: Basic configurations, sizing considerations, design strategy, 
design consideration for components. Compliant Structures: Basic 
configurations, sizing considerations, design strategy, design consideration 
9  

 
 
for 
components.

structures:

configuration, 
sizing 
considerations, design concepts for foundation, Material considerations for 
offshore structures 
4

methods, Transportation facilities and methods for different types of offshore 
structures, Installation methods for different offshore structures

SEMESTER S6 
SHIP PRODUCTION  
  
Course Code 
PENST631 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week (L: 
T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCNST502 
PBNST504 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand various types of shipyard layouts, material handling systems.  
2. Discern various production management methodologies in modern shipbuilding. 
3. Discern the various assembly techniques, welding symbols and standards used in shipbuilding. 
4. Explicate the various types of outfitting and launching methodologies adopted in modern 
shipbuilding. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
General principles for location and layout of shipyards. Functional and 
geographic aspects, transport, supply industry and human resource. Evolution of 
first to fourth generation shipyards and their typical layouts. Product and 
Process Oriented Work Breakdown Structure. Integrated hull construction, 
outfitting and painting (IHOP), grouping and work breakdown structure. Zone 
construction method for hull blocks, outfitting and painting, pipe piece family 
manufacturing. Material handling, storage and transport systems. Material 
preparation. Straightening of plates, sand blasting, painting, lofting, nesting. 
9  
2 
Production management. Pre-production, production and post production stages. 
Planning, design, production, material management. Quality control/ quality 
assurance. Accuracy control. Risk management. Project monitoring – build 
strategy, progress monitoring, PERT charts. Cutting processes and tools 
mechanical cutting, thermal cutting, general description of the various machines, 
photoelectric and NC-control devices. Bending of plates and sections. Heat-line 
bending 
9  

 
 
3 
Assembly of Ship’s Structure. Assembly jigs. Structural arrangement of the fore 
and aft end structure, superstructures, machinery foundation, cranes and davits. 
Welding in shipbuilding, welding methods, standards, symbols. Erection of 
ship’s hull. Handling of pre-assembled units in the erection area,  Different 
methods of hull assembly. Block erection methods – floor, ring and pyramid. 
Single/ multi point erection methods, Technological processes in  the installation 
of main machinery, shafting and propeller. 
9  
4 
Weld defects, distortions and their preventive measures. Testing – destructive/ 
non destructive. Launching- Mechanical Launching Methods (Slip, Lift), 
Construction of slipways for end launch and side launch. Launching curves. 
Arresting arrangements. Tipping, Pivoting/ plunging, drop off. Other Methods of 
launching - Launching by Floating Off (Building Dock, Floating Dock), 
Launching using air bags. 
9

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1.  Identify the operations in different outfitting departments. 
2. Explain various processes involved in the hull and machinery installation works.  
3. Understand the concept of design for production and need of quality control and assurance.  
4. Understand typical shipyard layout and productivity. 
SYLLABUS 
 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1

9  
2 
Technological process in the hull and machinery installation, technological process

outfitting.   
9

monitoring, shipyard capacity estimation, role of process and procedure in 
shipyard capacity evaluation, Shipyard layout, factors affecting design of shipyard 
layout, production facility layout, some aspects of shipyard capacity augmentation, 
developing shipbuilding strategy, Cost Estimation methods in ship production.

SEMESTER S6 
SHIP PRODUCTION MANAGEMENT 
  
Course Code 
PENST633 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week (L: 
T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand a standard ship production system. 
2. Discern production planning and control  for ship production activities 
3. Apply operation research, operation planning in shipbuilding process.  
4. Understand the information exchange during ship production .   
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Ship production systems, systems approach, subsystems, comprehensive 
system model, ship as a system, product standardization and work 
simplification, product mix,  quality assurance and quality control activities in 
shipyards, problems of accuracy, tolerances, standards, measuring techniques 
9  
2 
Production planning and control, planning for operations, interconnection 
between production design and process planning. production and process 
analysis, assembly charts, operation process charts, flow process charts,  
process selection, application of models for process planning, scheduling and 
control, Gantt charts, CPM & PERT, transportation models. 
9  
3 
Introduction to operation research, operation planning and control production 
planning scheduling network models, quality control maintenance analysis, 
production standards in several parts of the ship production process, work 
measurement systems, methods of man- hour determination. 
9 

 
 
4 
Information exchange during ship production - communication between 
departments and other stakeholders - classification society, regulatory body, 
ship owner, design office, Database Management Systems (DBMS) in ship 
production, the inventory problem, functions of inventory, inventory costs. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
SUBMARINES AND SUBMERSIBLES 
  
Course Code 
PENST634 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week (L: 
T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCNST205 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand the submersible System. 
2. Discern submarine hydrostatics. 
3. Understand submarine hydrodynamics. 
4. Understand the basic structural aspects and engineering systems of a submarine. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
The submersible system, basic design of manned submersibles, design 
objectives, characteristics and development of submersibles, environment – 
physical properties of sea water, dynamical processes 
9  
2 
Submarine hydrostatics, principles of flotation, submarines on the surface, 
arrangement of the main ballast tanks, submarine submerged, buoyancy 
elements, weight elements, trim and compensating tanks, special tanks, weight / 
space relationship, general form and arrangement 
9  
3 
Submarine hydrodynamics, Resistance, appendage resistance, sway and heave 
resistance, resistance estimation, propulsion, dynamics and control, equation of 
motion of a submarine, hydrodynamic derivatives, stability and control in the 
horizontal plane, stability and control in the vertical plane, steering and depth 
control system. 
9  

 
 
4 
Structure and systems,  submarine structure, operational requirement for depth, 
pressure hull design,  shape of the pressure vessel,  buckling deformation of the 
shell, failure modes, pressure hull penetration, diving and surfacing system,  
Hydraulic systems - high pressure air systems - water systems -systems for 
hydrostatic control - environmental control system - provision for escape, -
electrical systems. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
COMPUTATIONAL FLUID DYNAMICS IN MARINE TECHNOLOGY 
Course Code 
PENST635 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
 PCNST205 
PCNST302
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the governing flow equations for common flow problems and to understand 
discretisation  of a domain into a mesh 
2. Understand the boundary conditions to be applied. 
3. Understand numerical solution methods and their limitations and to understand the role of 
turbulence and its  influence on fluid flows 
4. Provide the student with a significant level of experience in the use of modern CFD software 
for the analysis of complex fluid-flow systems 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Computational Fluid Dynamics , CFD applications, 
numerical vs analytical vs experimental, modelling vs experimentation, 
fundamental principles of conservation, Reynolds transport theorem, 
conservation equations for mass, momentum and energy,  convective forms 
of the equations and general description 
 
9  
2 
Numerical methods for solving CFD problems, classification and overview 
of numerical methods,  classification into various types of equations such as 
parabolic, elliptic and hyperbolic, boundary and initial conditions,  overview 
of numerical methods, Finite Difference Method, Finite Element Method and 
Finite Volume Method 
 
9  
3 
The basic structure of a CFD code, pre-processor, solver and postprocessor, 
user-defined subroutines, numerical grid generation, transformation and 
mapping, solution to some basic problems in fluid flow – free surface flows 
and N-S equations around a body in water, numerical flow simulation. 
9  
4 
Features of turbulent flow, vorticity transport equation, general properties of 
 
9  

 
 
turbulent quantities, Reynolds Average Navier Stokes (RANS) equation, 
closure problem in turbulence, types of turbulence models like eddy 
viscosity models, mixing length model, turbulent kinetic energy and 
dissipation, κ-ε model, RNG κ-ε model and κ-ω model, Reynolds Stress 
Model (RSM), Large Eddy Simulation (LES), Direct Numerical Simulation 
(DNS).  
A minor CFD project in ship hydrodynamics using any commercial or open-
source CFD package. 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly defines the CFD problem. 
b. Examine and identify relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, 
objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and present a well-reasoned solution approach based on CFD. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with technical evidence. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions for flow problems. 
b. Compare trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Consider feasibility and practical implications. 

 
 
4. Design Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions. 
b. Successfully translate the chosen solution into tangible outputs. 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate 
for the problem. (K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 
understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S6 
SHIP DESIGN II 
Course Code 
PBNST604 
CIE Marks 
60 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PBNST504  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To enable the student to understand the standardization concept, cargo handling arrangements 
in ships and the design process of ship’s rudder 
2. To enable the student to understand the anchoring and mooring systems in ships and to 
determine the numbers and sizes of anchors, chains and mooring ropes 
3. To provide the student an understanding of ship design methodologies to design general 
arrangement of typical merchant ships 
4. To enable the student to understand the relevant regulations on life saving appliances and fire 
fighting appliances and to apply these regulations to typical merchant ships 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Standardisation, process and product standard. Cargo handling equipment, 
lifting devices. Cargo access, cargo hatches, design of hatch coamings. 
Steering gear, types, design aspects, design of rudder. 
9  
2 
Anchoring and mooring arrangement. Types of anchors, anchor chain, 
anchor windlass, capstan, chain stopper, hawse pipe, spurling pipe, design of 
chain locker, bitter end connection. Equipment number calculation. Mooring 
systems, mooring machinery, deck fittings and structural arrangement. 
9  
3 
Design of General Arrangement (GA) of a ship,factors influencing GA, 
subdivision of ship’s hull, superstructure and deckhouses, arrangement of 
cargo spaces, cargo handling arrangement, arrangement of machinery spaces, 
arrangement of accommodation and associated spaces, arrangement of tanks 
and other spaces.Accommodation standards, space allocation, modular 
arrangement.Access equipment, hatches, manholes, doors, other closing and 
9  

 
 
opening devices, load line rules on closing and opening devices, gangways 
and ladders.Guard rails and stanchions.  
4 
Lights and sound signals, navigational mast. Life Saving Appliances (LSA), 
international regulations on LSA.Fire Fighting Appliances (FFA), 
international regulations on FFA. Structural fire protection.  
Ventilation, insulation, lining, partitions, floor covering and painting in 
accommodation spaces.Air pipes and sounding pipes in tanks. Ventilators in 
holds. Sea inlets. 
9

CO2

the numbers and sizes of anchors, chains and mooring ropes  
K3 
CO3

typical merchant ships. 
K3 
CO4

fighting appliances applicable to ships and apply these regulations to 
typical merchant ships 
K3

2. Contribution in Progress Presentation and Question Answer Sessions (4 Marks) 
 
 Individual contribution to the presentation  
 Effectiveness in answering questions and handling feedback  
3. Involvement in the Project Work and Team Work (3 Marks) 
 
 Active participation and individual contribution  
 Teamwork and collaboration

 Application of theoretical knowledge and problem-solving  
 Final Result

 Effectiveness in answering questions

SEMESTER S6 
FUNDAMENTALS OF FLOATING BODIES 
Course Code 
OENST611 
CIE Marks 
           40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
          60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
   2 Hrs 30 Min 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
       Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Acquire knowledge on various types of floating bodies such as ships. 
2. Develop fundamental concepts of Naval Architecture. 
3. Identify various types of materials used for construction of floating bodies and to identify 
various major and minor structural components of a ship. 
4. Identify various main and auxiliary machineries onboard a vessel. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
 
 
Types of ships,  classification, cargo ships, general cargo ships, bulk 
carriers, container ships, ro-ro ships, barge carriers, tankers, fishing 
vessels, factory ships, supply ships, cable ships, ice breakers, research 
vessels, and warships, high speed crafts such as hydrofoils, air cushion 
vehicles etc, small pleasure crafts like  yachts, ketches, etc, the ship's form, 
main dimensions and hydrostatic particulars, lines plan, form coefficients. 
 
6 
2 
Physical fundamentals and forces acting on a ship - Archimedes principle, 
laws of floatation, stability of floating bodies, six degrees of freedom, 
forces acting on a ship in static condition and in waves, heel, trim, 
hydrostatic parameters, basic stability parameters. 
 
9  
3 
Shipbuilding Materials and their properties, compositions, introduction to 
ship structural members, structural components such as bottom structure, 
shell plating and framing, decks, hatches and hatch covers, superstructures, 
bulkheads, tanks, holds, fore and aft structure, stern and rudder. 
9 

 
 
4 
Propulsion machinery - development of ship propulsion, main engines - 
diesel engines, steam engines & turbines, gas turbines, diesel-electric drive, 
nuclear power plants, auxiliary machinery- power supply, auxiliary engines 
for ship, auxiliary engines for engine plant operation, steering gear 
 
12

SEMESTER S6 
MARINE MATERIALS, CORROSION PREVENTION AND 
PROTECTION 
 
Course Code 
OENST612 
CIE Marks 
           40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
          60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
 2 Hrs 30 Min 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
        Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Discern the Evolution of marine materials  
2. Understand types of corrosion of marine structures 
3. Discern effective methods of material preservation and corrosion prevention  
4. Understand the measures to be taken in design stage to minimise corrosion in marine 
structures. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction 
to 
different 
types 
of 
materials 
used 
in 
marine 
construction/shipbuilding, Material fabrication and service requirement, 
Classification society requirements, Types of shipbuilding quality steels, 
Mild steels, normal strength steels (A, B, D, E classes),  High Tensile 
Steels (HTS) grades, High Strength Low Alloy (HSLA), Aluminium 
alloys, alloy designation, welding requirements, Strength of aluminium 
compared to steel, Composition of aluminium alloys used in ship building, 
Advantages of using aluminium over steel in ship building. 
 
9  
2 
Types of Corrosion in Marine Environment, Corrosion Identification, 
Factors affecting Corrosion. Types of steel and tendency of corrosion in 
various types of steel, corrosion of Titanium and Nickel alloys, Copper and 
Copper based alloys, Zinc, Aluminium and its alloys. Corrosion on 
propeller, marine machinery and deck fittings. 
 
8  
3 
Material storage and preservation in shipyard, treatment of steel in 
shipyards. degreasing, weathering, mechanical surface cleaning, pickling, 
blast cleaning, flame cleaning. rust converters, chemical pre-treatment and 
11 

 
 
comparison of pre-treatment methods. 
Paint schemes in ships and marine structures, classification of paints- 
common paint vehicles, drying oils, oleo-resins, alkyd resins, polymerizing 
chemicals and bitumen. Role of constituents of paints. suitability of each 
for various applications. typical paint schemes for underwater areas, boot 
top above water, weather decks, superstructures and tanks interiors 
4 
Corrosion control - importance of corrosion protection, measures to 
minimise corrosion, corrosion control by design, corrosion inhibitors. 
cathodic protection- mechanism of cathodic protection, sacrificial anode, 
design of sacrificial anode system for ships and marine structures, 
advantages and disadvantages of sacrificial anode system. impressed 
current cathodic protection system in ships 
 
8

SEMESTER S6 
MARINE POLLUTION 
Course Code 
OENST613 
CIE Marks 
              40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
              60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
      2 Hrs 30 Min 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
            Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand different sources of marine pollution including ships and floating structures, their 
impact on the marine environment. 
2. Select suitable methods to control the marine pollution in different operating conditions 
3. Apply various strategies and methods for marine pollution recovery to minimise 
environmental impact. 
4. Understand role of various international and regional rules and regulations for marine 
environmental protection in design of ships. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Definition of Marine Pollution, Types of Marine Pollution, Various Sources 
of Marine Pollution, Marine Pollution in the Coastal Zone, Pollution from 
ships and offshore assets  
Concerns and Consequences of Marine Pollution - Global Warming, Sea 
Level Changes, Carbon Emissivity and Green Shipping Biodiversity 
 
9 
2 
Prevention of air and water pollution from Ships, Emissions from Ships 
Engines, Fuel Oil Quality, Requirements for Survey and Issuance of 
International Air Pollution Prevention Certificate (IAPP), Oil Pollution, 
Segregated Ballast Tanks, Oily Water Separator, Ballast Water 
Management (BWM) Convention 
 
9  
3 
Introduction to Marine Oil Pollution Recovery Systems: Types of Recovery 
Systems, Skimming Systems, Oil storage system, Treatment of pollutant 
after recovery. 
9  

 
 
4 
IMO Marine Engine Regulations, Requirements for Survey and Issuance of 
International Air Pollution Prevention Certificate (IAPP), Energy 
Efficiency Design Index (EEDI), Ship Energy Efficiency Management Plan 
(SEEMP), Survey and Issuance of International Sewage Pollution 
Prevention Certificates (ISPP) 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
BASIC SHIP STRUCTURES 
Course Code 
OENST614 
CIE Marks 
             40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
            60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
   2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
       Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Discern shipbuilding materials, role of classification societies and ship framing systems 
2. Understand the shell and bottom structures of a ship 
3. Discern basic structural drawings and understand the structure of bulkheads and tanks 
4. Understand the structure of decks, superstructures and the end structures 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Shipbuilding materials, wood, steel, stress-strain diagrams, higher tensile 
steel, aluminium alloys, proof stress, GRP and FRP 
Classification societies, longitudinal and transverse strength. 
Framing system, longitudinal, transverse and combined framing, basic 
structural components - primary and, secondary stiffeners 
 
9  
2 
Bottom construction, single and double bottom, functions, inner bottom 
plating, floors, transversely and  longitudinally framed double bottom, 
additional stiffening in critical areas, testing of double bottom 
compartments, foundations 
Shell plating- bottom shell plating, side shell plating, additional stiffening 
for panting, navigation in ice, bilge keel 
 
9 
3 
Typical ship structural drawings such as midship section, shell expansion, 
structural profile. 
Bulkheads, spacing of watertight bulkheads, construction of watertight 
bulkheads, testing of watertight bulkheads, watertight doors. 
Tanks, deep tanks, testing of deep tanks, topside tanks, shaft tunnel 
9 

 
 
4 
Decks and superstructure, deck plating, deck stiffening, pillars, hatch 
coamings, 
hatch 
covers, 
bulwarks, 
forecastle, 
poop 
structure, 
superstructures and deck houses, weather tight doors. 
Fore end structure, stem, bulbous bows, chain locker, hawse pipes, bow 
thruster units, aft end structure, stern construction, stern frame, rudders, 
steering gear; stern tube, shaft bossing, P and A brackets 
 
9

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test understanding 
of the upcoming experiment. 
 Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of the 
theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper documentation 
of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record.

4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles during 
a viva voce session. 
 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, 
and record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
 Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or programming 
task. 
 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality of 
program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the subject. 
 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

SEMESTER S7 
JOINING TECHNIQUES IN SHIPBUILDING TECHNOLOGY 
  
Course Code 
PENST741 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PENST641 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Explain types of welding, welding process and welding parameters used in shipbuilding. 
2. Discern various special welding arrangements in modern shipbuilding. 
3. Discern the radiant welding, underwater welding and robotic welding used in shipbuilding. 
4. Explicate the various types of weld defects and testing in modern shipbuilding. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to various joining techniques in ship building industry. Understand 
welding and classification of welding Fuel gases, GMAW process, different 
metal transfers and shielding gas. Different types of oxy-acetylene flames, Fore 
hand and back hand welding techniques. Function of fillers and fluxes. Carbon 
arc welding, Shielded metal arc, submerged arc, TIG, MIG, Electro slag, Electro 
gas, Plasma arc, arc spot welding, stud welding 
9 
2 
Principle, welding arrangements and advantages/ disadvantages of resistance 
welding, spot welding, seam welding, projection welding, resistance upset 
welding, flash butt, percussion welding, tube welding, high frequency welding, 
solid state welding, cold welding, diffusion welding, ultrasonic welding, 
explosive, friction and inertia welding, thermo-chemical welding (thermit and 
atomic hydrogen welding. Forging, 
11 
3 
Radiant energy welding (electron beam and laser beam). Under water welding.  
Wet, dry, hyper baric and cavity welding. Welding arrangements and special 
precautions to be taken. Robotic Welding. Application of Robotic Welding in 
Ship Production, Types of Welding Robots and their control system. Brazing and 
10 

 
 
soldering. Difference between brazing, soldering and welding. Adhesives and 
bonding methods. 
4 
Weld Defects and distortion control. Tests destructive/ non-destructive. Welding 
performance and procedure qualification, test reports, acceptance Standards. 
Variables essential/ non-essential. Consumable Classification & Coding. 
Crystallization of a Pure Metal, Phase Transformation in Iron-Carbon Diagram 
7

SEMESTER S7 
COMPOSITE BOAT DESIGN 
Course Code 
PENST742 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand composition and processing of composite materials. 
2. Explain various processes of composite boat construction.  
3. Understand mechanical and structural properties of composites. 
4. Undertake structural design and analysis of composite ships. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to composite materials, history of fibre reinforced composites, 
constituent materials, fibres, matrix, fillers, additives, properties of typical 
composite materials, application of composites, processing FRP  
composites, molding,  spray  up,  hand  lay-up,  compression moulding, 
matched dies moulding, forming methods employing gas pressure, low 
pressure closed moulding, pultrusion, filament winding. 
9 
2 
FRP boat construction, single skin, sandwich construction, types of frames 
(top hat, with or without core), bulkhead, typical midship section of FRP 
boat, connections, hull to deck, bulkhead to hull, hull moulding, deck 
moulding, environmental control, temperature and humidity control, FRP 
boat construction quality control, destructive and non destructive testing 
 
 
9 
3 
Micro mechanical analysis, volume and weight fractions, longitudinal 
strength and stiffness, transverse section modulus, shear modulus, 
Poisson‘s ratio, structural analysis, elastic properties of unidirectional 
lamina, stress strain relationships, analysis of laminated composites, basic 
assumptions,  stress- displacement / stress-strain relationship, coupling 
effect, types of laminate configuration (symmetric, anti-symmetric) 
 
 
9 

 
 
4 
Structural design of FRP boats, basic structural arrangement using 
classification society rules, Determination of boat shell lamination using 
classification society rules, Determination of stiffener lamination and size 
using classification society rules. 
 
 
9

SEMESTER S7 
REFRIGERATION AND AIR CONDITIONING OF SHIPS 
 
Course Code 
PENST743 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand basic principles of refrigeration on board ships. 
2. Explain details of refrigerating machinery.  
3. Understand basic principles of air-conditioning on-board ships.  
4. Understand standards for marine air conditioning systems. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction, marine applications of mechanical refrigeration, refrigerated 
ship's stores refrigeration at sea, cargoes and carrying conditions, 
thermodynamical principles vapour, compression cycles (CARNOT, 
superheating, subcooling, multistage operation), absorption cycles. 
 
9 
2 
Refrigerating machinery, principal components, compressors, condensers, 
evaporators, regulators. refrigerant properties- demands, choice, safety, 
lubricants, refrigerant numbering system, alternative refrigerants, 
secondary refrigerants, methods of cooling- cargo chamber cooling in 
conventional reefers, methods of cooling containers, insulations, heat 
leakage estimation, total load on the refrigeration plant 
 
10 
3 
Air conditioning fundamentals, definitions, psychrometric chart, air 
conditioning (heating), heat sources, heat exchangers, heat pump, air 
conditioning (cooling), principal arrangement and equipment. 
7 
4 
Standards for marine air conditioning systems, air flow & air conditioning 
capacity calculations, air conditioning systems, HVAC systems and 
components- single zone system, multiple zone systems, terminal reheat 
system, dual duct system, variable air volume systems, water systems, 
unitary systems, cargo hold dehumidification systems. 
 
10

SEMESTER S7 
DESIGN OF MACHINE ELEMENTS 
Course Code 
PENST744 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs 30 Mins 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand basic principles of design of machine elements. 
2. Explain details of  joints.  
3. Understand basic principles of drive elements and shaft couplings.  
4. Understand  standards bearings and gears 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of machine design, definitions, design process, design 
principles, design criteria, stresses in machine parts-working stress, safe 
stress, factor of safety, endurance limits, fatigue factors elastic springs-
classification and uses of springs-allowable stresses and deflections-
design for fluctuating loads 
 
9 
2 
Joints,  principles of force transmission, detachable joints (pins, keys, 
spline and bolted joints), non detachable joints, welded, soldered and 
glued joints, riveted joints, strength of welded and riveted joints. 
 
8 
3 
Drive elements, shafts,  torsion and bending of shafts, design of shafts for 
strength and deflection, effect of key ways, crank shafts, shaft couplings, 
rigid  coupling  (flange  and  compression  couplings), couplings with 
kinematics flexibility slip couplings, fluid couplings. 
9 
4 
Bearings, slide bearings-introduction to lubrication, hydrodynamic 
bearings, bearing materials, design of slide bearings. roller bearings, 
types, static & dynamic load, capacity, bearing life and selection of 
bearings. gears: - types (spur and parallel helical gears) and function of 
gears, strength of gear teeth, stresses and stress concentration in gears-
design of gears. 
 
10

SEMESTER S7 
DESIGN OF HIGH SPEED CRAFTS 
Course Code 
PENST745 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PBNST504 
PBNST604
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand the requirements for high speed craft market. 
2. Develop the dimensions and hull form for high speed craft. 
3. Select the propulsion package for the selected ship  
4. Optimise the structure of high speed craft 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction: Basic differences between conventional and high-performance 
crafts ,  special features, types, monohull , planning craft, hydrofoil craft , air 
cushion vehicles, multihulls – catamaran – trimaran, SWATH vessels, 
Unconventional hulls 
 
7  
2 
Hull forms, aero and hydrodynamic forces, stability criteria, resistance of 
very slender hulls, in particular importance of form factors, transom stern 
effects prediction of form factors for transom stern vessels, effect of water 
depth on HSE resistance. 
 
8 
3 
Resistance prediction methods for HSC, regression methods, , thin strip 
theory, assumptions, approximation, CFD, hybrid methods, powering and 
propulsion, 
seaworthiness, 
maneuvering 
and 
control, 
comparative 
performance and applications of propulsion devices of water jets and other 
devices 
12 
4 
Structural design of high-speed craft,  slamming loads and structure 
responses,  materials and structures,  structural design philosophy,  modeling 
and analysis, class society rules 
 
9 

 
 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5
15
10
10
40
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
Criteria for evaluation: 
 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly define owner’s requirements of a high speed craft 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, 
objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Analyse the owners requirements and bring out possible dimensions as solution 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with technical evidence. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compare trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Consider feasibility and practical implications. 
4. Design Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible design by implementing the proposed solutions. 
b. Successfully translate the chosen solution into tangible outputs. 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which design  is most appropriate for the 
problem. (K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
Scoring: 
 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 

 
 
understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S7 
OCEAN WAVE HYDRODYNAMICS  
  
Course Code 
PENST751 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCNST302 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand the Ocean environment, graphical and mathematical representation of waves 
2. Discern various types of wave loads on structures 
3. Understand wave theories 
4. Discern wave deformations and understand random wave theory  
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Wave Motion : Classification of Waves, Derivation of the Velocity Potential, 
Dispersion Relationship, Celerity in Different Water Depth Conditions, Local 
Fluid Particle Velocities and Acceleration Under Progressive Waves, Water 
Particle Displacement Under Progressive Waves, Pressure Distribution Under 
Progressive Waves, Group Celerity, Wave Energy, Wave Power, Simple 
Problems on Wave Motion. 
9 
2 
Wave Loads: Force Regimes, Design Wave Approach, Morison Equation- Fixed 
Cylinder in Waves, Fixed Cylinder in Waves and Current, Flexible Cylinder in 
Waves, Wave Forces on an Inclined Cylinder, Wave Force on a Vertical Cylinder 
in Deep water, Wave Forces on Piles in Shallow Water, Submarine Pipelines, 
Froude-Krylov Forces, Diffraction Regime, Simple Problems on Wave Loads. 
9 
3 
Finite Amplitude Waves: Stoke’s Wave Theory- Comparison Between Wave 
Theories, Solitary Wave Theory, Cnoidal Wave Theory, Stream Function Theory, 
Simple Problems on Finite Amplitude Waves. 
9 

 
 
4 
Wave Deformation: Wave Refraction, Wave Diffraction, Wave Breaking- Types 
of Wave Breaking, Waves on Currents, Simple Problems on Wave Deformation, 
Random Waves: Generation of Ocean Waves, Importance of Study of Wave 
Data, Collection of Wave Data, Analysis of Ocean Waves- Statistical Method, 
Spectral Method, Fast Fourier Transform Method, Irregular Sea Way- Wave-
Wave Spectrum Relationship (Theory Only). 
9

SEMESTER S7 
COMPUTER AIDED SHIP DESIGN 
 
Course Code 
PENST 752 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PBNST 504 
PBNST 604 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand Computer aided Ship Design Process. 
2. Discern Numerical representation method of Hull form and Ship Geometry. 
3. Demonstrate CAD Tool in developing preliminary faired lines design for hull form generation 
and presenting in 3D form. 
4. Apply optimization techniques in generating basic data in development of detailed design from 
preliminary design. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Numerical Techniques in Computer Aided Ship Design - Numerical 
Interpolation: Differences, Newton‘s Forward Difference interpolation formula, 
Lagrangian Interpolation formula. Numerical Integration: Integration formulas. 
Curve Fitting: Fitting of Polynomials, Least Square curve fitting technique, 
choosing the degree of the polynomial, Ill-conditioning difficulties, Orthogonal 
Polynomial fitting 
9 
2 
Preliminary Ship Design, Preliminary Parameter Estimation: Displacement, 
Length, Breadth, Depth, Draught, Block Coefficient, Check on Transverse & 
longitudinal Stability, Freeboard, etc., Estimation of Power, Capacity, Basic Ship 
Method, Computer Aided Preliminary Ship Design: Preliminary Parameter 
Selection,  
11 
3 
Lines Design and Fairing: Manual Graphical method, Computer Aided Curve 
fitting Techniques Fairing Principles, Spline Fitting: Cubic Spline curve, Bezier 
Curve, B-Spline Curve. 
10 

 
 
4 
Optimisation Methods in Ship Design Introduction-Modelling of Design as 
Optimisation, Different 
Optimisation 
Methods, Linear and Non-liner 
optimization, Application to Ship Design 
7

SEMESTER S7 
FINITE ELEMENT ANALYSIS IN NAVAL ARCHITECTURE  
   
Course Code 
PENST753 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCNST403 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand basics of finite element methods 
2. Discern finite element fundamentals like shape functions, convergence, stiffness matrix etc 
3. Understand FEA applications in ship structural analysis 
4. Discern pre processing, processing and post processing considerations in ship structural analysis. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Scope of finite element method in solving  engineering problems, General steps 
in finite element analysis, variational formulations and weighted residual 
methods, Analysis of trusses, beams, and frames, Analysis of plates, Analysis of 
three-dimensional problems 
9 
2 
Shape functions, Convergence criteria, General equations for calculation of 
stiffness matrix, Derivation of stiffness matrix for truss beam, Plane stress, 
plane strain, axisymmetric elements. 
9 
3 
Ship Structural Analysis using FEM- formulation of plate finite elements, issues 
associated with plate formulation of finite elements. Numerical examples on 
simple plate analysis. One dimensional and two dimensional finite element 
modelling of ship structure 
9 
4 
Preprocessing - preliminary checks, engineering model checks - analysis type 
and assumptions, geometry assumptions, material properties, stiffness and mass 
properties, loads and boundary conditions,  finite element model checks, 
element types, mesh design, substructures and sub-modelling, FE model loads 
and boundary conditions, processing, post processing – methods, displacement 
results, stress results, fatigue and fracture results 
9

SEMESTER S7 
DESIGN OF FISHING VESSELS 
  
Course Code 
PENST754 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Acquire basic knowledge on fishing vessels and systems onboard. 
2. Understand basic design procedure of fishing vessels 
3. Understand resistance and propulsion performance characteristics of fishing vessels. 
4. Understand basic structural design concepts of fishing vessels. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction: definitions of fishing vessel, special features of fishing 
vessels, regulations for the safety of fishing vessels, classification of 
fishing vessels, Characteristics of fish ground; Fishing gear and 
methods, drift net, long line, drag net, siene net, dredging, with electric 
light, harpoon/whale catching, trawling (side and stern trawlers, single 
and pair trawling, pelagic &bottom trawling). 
9 
2 
Design Procedure: Owner‘s specifications, Economy, fuel efficiency, hull form, 
investment cost, operating revenues and costs. Design of Main Dimensions and 
form: parent vessel data analysis, space requirement (capacity) of the whole 
ship, estimation of main dimensions, estimation of form coefficients, estimation 
of light ship weight, estimation of dead weight, design of lines. General 
arrangement: Engine room, fish holds, erections, deck machinery arrangement, 
crew accommodation, fuel, fresh-water, ballast tanks, bulkhead positions. 
9 
3 
Resistance, powering and propeller selection: friction resistance, wave making 
resistance, eddy resistance, net resistance, powering calculations, propeller 
selection, Propulsion Systems and other machinery/equipment, different 
9 

 
 
propulsion systems and selection  of main    engine,    selection    of   
equipment‘s/instruments    for    fish    finding,    navigation, communication, 
firefighting, lifesaving and net monitoring Seakeeping and manoeuvring 
considerations 
4 
Material and construction methods: mechanical properties of  materials,  
comparison  of hulls of different material, type of construction, details of steel 
construction, structural design methods, construction methods in FRP/GRP, 
Aluminium and Ferro-cement. 
9 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks)

SEMESTER S7 
RENEWABLE ENERGY IN MARITIME SECTOR 
  
Course Code 
PENST755 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand ocean renewable energy sources. 
2. Discern the tidal energy sources and power generation 
3. Explore the offshore wind energy sources and power generation 
4. Explore the wave energy sources, OTEC and power generation 
SYLLABUS 
 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
The global energy mix, climate change & sustainability, Introduction to ocean 
energy sources and types, Methods for ocean observations: Water level 
Measurements - Tidal poles, tidal gauges, pressure sensors, Radar sensors. 
Current measurements, Wave measurements  
9 
2 
Tidal Energy, Tide generating forces, progressive waves, Cotidal charts, 
standing waves, resonance, Coriolis forces, Kelvin Waves, tidal analysis & 
prediction, compound tides, over tides and tidal asymmetry, characterizing tides 
at site and power density, tidal stream devices, basic hydrodynamics of 
horizontal axis turbines and power coefficients & Betz limit, tidalrange: lagoons 
and barrages. 
9 
3 
Offshore Wind Energy, introduction and history of offshore wind energy, 
offshore wind turbines, aerodynamics of wind turbines, power curves, 
assessment of wind energy at site, case study with calculation of power output & 
capacity factor, marine spatial planning. 
9 

 
 
4 
Wave Energy and Other forms of Ocean Energy, Wave processes, linear wave 
theory, dispersion equation, wave energy & wave power, irregular & nonlinear 
waves, wave transformation due to shoaling water, wave energy convertors, 
wave resource assessment, ocean currents, Ocean Thermal Energy Conversion 
(OTEC): Closed & open cycle, Environmental impacts of OTEC, Salinity 
gradients 
9 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5
15
10
10
40
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
Criteria for evaluation: 
 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly define a renewable energy problem in marine environment 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, 
objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and present a well-reasoned solution approach for the renewable 
energy problem.. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with technical evidence. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compare trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Consider feasibility and practical implications. 
4. Design Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions. 
b. Successfully translate the chosen solution into tangible outputs. 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 

 
 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate for 
the problem. (K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
 
Scoring: 
 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 
understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S7 
BASIC PRINCIPLES OF MARINE VESSEL DESIGN 
 
Course Code 
OENST721
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs 30 Mins 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. To introduce the structure of international marine industry and the economical aspects  
in ship design to the student 
2. To provide the students an understanding of the methodologies for preliminary design of 
ships  
3. To provide the students an understanding of the ship design methodologies to develop 
lines plans of typical merchant ships 
4. To enable the student to understand the relevant regulations on freeboard, tonnage and 
stability applicable to ships and to apply these regulations to typical merchant ships 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Types of ships: - terms and definitions, cargo ships (general cargo ships, 
bulk carriers, container ships, Ro-Ro ships, barge carriers, tankers), fishing 
vessels, factory ships, supply ships, Cable ships, ice breakers, research 
vessels, warships, hydrofoils, air cushion vehicles, small pleasure crafts 
(yachts, ketches, etc). Phases of ship design, design spiral. Ship 
parameters, deadweight, displacement, deadweight coefficient, hold 
capacity, stowage factor. 
9 
2 
Weight equation and volume equation and solution. Basic design procedure 
for main categories of ships, deadweight carriers, capacity carriers, linear 
dimension ships, special purpose ships. Procedure for selection of main 
dimensions and form coefficients. Estimation of weight, lightship weight, 
11 

 
 
steel weight, machinery weight, outfit weight, deadweight.  
General Arrangement (GA), factors influencing GA, subdivision of ship’s 
hull, superstructure and deckhouses, arrangement of cargo spaces, cargo 
handling arrangement, arrangement of machinery spaces, accommodation 
and associated spaces, tanks, and other spaces. 
3 
Ship’s lines plan, conventional method of lines design, lines design using 
existing lines plan, lines design using standard series, hull form section 
shapes, form of bow, bulbous bow, form of stern. Effect of hull form on 
ship’s performance. 
10 
4 
Freeboard and load line regulations. Stability and trim, watertight integrity. 
IMO regulations, intact stability criteria, damage stability criteria. Stability 
booklet. Tonnage regulations, gross tonnage, net tonnage. 
7

SEMESTER S7 
FUNDAMENTALS OF OFFSHORE STRUCTURES 
 
Course Code 
OENST722 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand the basics features of offshore structures 
2. Discern the basic principles of fixed offshore platform design 
3. Discern the basic principles of Compliant offshore  structures design 
4. Understand the basics of offshore installation. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Definition and functions of Offshore structures, Brief Historical 
Development,  Different types of Offshore Structure Configurations: Bottom 
Supported Fixed  Structures, Compliant Structures, Floating Structures and 
Novel & Small Field Offshore Structures, Offshore field development 
concepts and design phases 
9 
2 
Wave force on offshore structures: Small diameter and large diameter 
structures, vertical and arbitrarly oriented cylindrical members, Ocean 
currents and current forces exerted on offshore structures, Wind forces, 
Earthquake forces, Ice forces and Tides, Response of offshore structures to 
ocean environment, Introduction to corrosion and protection of offshore 
structures 
9 
3 
Design spiral, Various types of loads acting on offshore structures, 
Introduction to design tools for offshore structure design, Jacket structure: 
Basic configuration, sizing considerations, design strategy, bracing system, 
jacket design, pile design, deck design, top sides, appurtenances, Floating 
Structures: Basic configurations, design strategy, design consideration for 
components. 
Compliant 
Structures: 
Basic 
configurations, 
sizing 
9 

 
 
considerations, design strategy, design consideration for components. 
Gravity structures: Basic configuration, sizing considerations, design 
concepts for foundation, Material considerations for offshore structures 
4 
Introduction to construction of various types of offshore structures, Load out 
methods, Transportation facilities and methods for different types of offshore 
structures, Installation methods for different offshore structures 
9

SEMESTER S7 
BASICS OF DESIGN OF SUBMERSIBLES 
Course Code 
OENST723 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand the submersible System. 
2. Discern submarine hydrostatics. 
3. Understand submarine hydrodynamics. 
4. Understand the basic structural aspects and engineering systems of a submarine. 
SYLLABUS 
 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
The submersible system, basic design of manned submersibles, design 
objectives, characteristics and development of submersibles, environment – 
physical properties of sea water, dynamical processes 
6 
2 
Submarine hydrostatics, principles of flotation, submarines on the surface, 
arrangement of the main ballast tanks, submarine submerged, buoyancy 
elements, weight elements, trim and compensating tanks, special tanks, 
weight / space relationship, general form and arrangement 
 
9 
3 
Submarine hydrodynamics, Resistance, appendage resistance, sway and 
heave resistance, resistance estimation, propulsion, dynamics and control, 
equation of motion of a submarine, hydrodynamic derivatives, stability and 
control in the horizontal plane, stability and control in the vertical plane, 
steering and depth control system. 
9 

 
 
4 
Structure and systems, submarine structure, operational requirement for 
depth, pressure hull design, shape of the pressure vessel, buckling 
deformation of the shell, failure modes, pressure hull penetration, diving 
and surfacing system, Hydraulic systems - high pressure air systems - water 
systems -systems for hydrostatic control - environmental control system - 
provision for escape, -electrical systems. 
 
12

SEMESTER S7 
BASICS OF SHIP CONSTRUCTION 
Course Code 
OENST724 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand various types of shipyard layouts, material handling systems.  
2. Discern various production management methodologies in modern shipbuilding. 
3. Discern the various assembly techniques, welding symbols and standards used in 
shipbuilding. 
4. Explicate the various types of outfitting and launching methodologies adopted in modern 
shipbuilding. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
General principles for location and layout of a shipyard, evolution of 
shipyards – first  to fourth generation shipyards and their typical layouts, 
management of shipyard organisation structure – Product Oriented Work 
Breakdown Structure, Process Oriented Work Breakdown Structure, 
Integrated Hull construction, Outfitting and Painting (IHOP), grouping and 
work breakdown structure, zone construction method for hull blocks, 
outfitting and painting, storage and preparation of material - straightening 
of plates and rolled sections, sand blasting, painting, lofting, nesting. 
9 
2 
Production management – planning, design , production, quality, material 
management commercial activities, human resource, quality control, 
quality assurance, accuracy control, project life cycle, project monitoring – 
build strategy, progress monitoring, PERT charts,  cutting, bending and 
welding of steel plates and frames, fabrication of component parts, cutting 
9 

 
 
processes and tools, general description of the various machines, 
photoelectric and NC control devices, edge preparation, bending of rolled 
and built up sections - control of the bending process, automation of 
bending, plate bending, uniaxial bending, biaxial bending devices, cold 
bending, heat-line bending 
3 
Assembly of Ship’s Structure, sub-assemblies- built up T bars, web frames, 
machine foundations etc, welding deformation and straightening,  
prefabrication of flat sections, pre-assembly of biaxial stiffened panels, 
assembly of various components,  assembly of flat and corrugated sections, 
flat sections with curvature, double bottom sections,  assembly jigs, 
structural arrangement of the fore and aft end structure, superstructures, 
machinery foundation, technological processes in the hull installation the 
installation of main machinery, shafting and propeller, auxiliary machinery, 
welding in shipbuilding. 
9 
4 
Erection of hull and launching, handling of pre-assembled units in the 
erection area, Hull assembly – different methods of hull assembly. Block 
erection methods – floor, ring and pyramid. Single/ multi point erection 
methods, Technological processes in the installation of main machinery, 
shafting and propeller, auxiliary machinery, Welding- Weld defects, 
distortions and their preventive measures. Testing – destructive/ non-
destructive, Launching- Mechanical Launching Methods (Slip, Lift), 
Construction of slipways for end launch and side launch. Launching curves. 
Arresting arrangements, Tipping, Pivoting/ plunging. Drop off, Other 
Methods of launching - Launching by Floating Off (Building Dock, 
Floating Dock), Launching using air bags. 
9

SEMESTER S8 
SHIP SURVEY, ESTIMATION AND REPAIR   
 
Course Code 
PENST861 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCNST502 
PBNST504
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand the requirement and various types of marine surveys.  
2. Understand the different types of ship repair afloat. 
3. Understand ship repairs in dry dock. 
4. Discern the principles of work estimates and cost estimates. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to Marine Survey: Definition of Elementary Terminologies like 
Survey Authority, Recognized Organization, Port State control, Flag State 
control, Various Types of Marine Surveys - Initial Survey, Annual Survey, 
Periodic Survey, Intermediate Survey, Renewal Survey, Additional Survey. 
Survey During Transfer of Ships. Marine Surveying Agencies- Roles and 
Responsibilities of classification societies, Statutory Surveys – Role of MMD, 
IWAI. 
Marine Cargo Survey- Dry, Liquid and Container Cargoes. 
9  
2 
Afloat Repairs, Introduction, Causes of Wear and Damage in Ship’s Hull. 
Comparison Between Different Types of Repair Activities (Afloat, Berthed etc.) 
Testing for Water Tightness and Hull Continuity. Repair of hull and other Parts 
While Afloat. Underwater Welding – Welding Equipment, Quality Control and 
Standards; Degree of Automation 
9  

 
 
3 
Dry docking and repairing, Dry-docking- Steps to be Taken Before, During and 
After Dry-docking, Replacement of Hull Plates and Stiffeners, Decks and 
Bulkheads, Repair of Stem and Stern Frames and Shaft Bracket, Propeller Shaft 
Sealing Equipment, Rudder– pintle Clearances, Maintenance of Sea Water 
Suction and Overboard Valves, Safety During Repair – Various Operations 
Involving Risk, Safety Devices and Plans. 
9  
4 
Work and Cost Estimation, Work Estimation: Dry-docking Works - Docking and 
Undocking, Hull Preparation, Hull Painting, Propeller Works, Chain Lockers, 
Steel Works, Planning Charts, Shipbuilding Contracts, Costing and Estimation- 
Difference between Cost and Price, Top Down and Bottom Top Approaches in 
Costing, Demarcations and Subdivisions of Costs, Structural Costs, Outfit 
Costs, Labour Costs, Machinery Costs. 
9

No.

Quality Standards and Auditing in shipyards, Overview on ISO standard in Ship 
Building, Qualification Standards, Training and Certification, Quality Manual 
and Document Management, Quality in Planning, Design and Operation, 
Quality Policy of Shipyards.

SEMESTER S8 
MARITIME LAW AND SHIPPING MANAGEMENT 
Course Code 
PENST863 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCNST205  
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the role of international conventions in formulating Maritime Law, the roles of 
Maritime Labour Convention and international conventions on the Law of the Sea. 
2. Understand the roles of international conventions for the Safety of Life at Sea, International 
Ship and Port Facility Security Code (ISPS Code) and other conventions 
3. To enable the student to understand the basic structure of shipping industry and the role of 
various stakeholders in the industry 
4. To provide the student an understanding of shipping economics and the shipping market 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to maritime law; need and source of maritime law; 
implementation of maritime law through national legislation; role of United 
Nations (UN), International Maritime Organization (IMO) and International 
Labour Organization (ILO); role of Flag state and Port state in 
implementation of law; introduction to SOLAS, MARPOL, STCW and 
Maritime Labour Convention (MLC); need of survey and certification. 
Classification Societies, need and role of Classification Societies. United 
Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea (UNCLOS), various zones and 
limits. 
Maritime Labour Convention, minimum requirements for seafarers to work 
on a ship, conditions of employment, accommodation, recreational facilities, 
food and catering, Health protection, medical care, welfare and social 
security. 
9 

 
 
2 
SOLAS, Introduction to SOLAS, Subdivision and stability, Fire protection, 
detection and extinction, Life saving appliances and arrangements, Carriage 
of grain, Carriage of dangerous goods.  
Load Line Convention, important definitions and markings, survey and 
certification. 
ISPS Code, ship security plan, security levels, declaration of security, ship 
security alert system, piracy, best management practices to deter piracy. 
Introduction to other Conventions; International Convention on Salvage, 
Convention on Limitation of Liability for Maritime Claims; Oil Pollution 
Compensation Conventions. 
9 
3 
Shipping Management- Types of cargoes, types of ships which carry them, 
Ship’s tonnages (GT, NT), Cargo carrying capacity. Ship registration, ship 
insurance. Ship owners, operators and managers. Types of shipping services, 
liner and tramp. Role of intermediaries in shipping business- freight brokers, 
clearing and forwarding agents, stevedores, shipbrokers, bunker and stores 
suppliers, shipping agencies. 
9 
4 
Shipping Economics-Sea transport and the global economy, role of shipping 
in economic development. Shipping market cycles, shipping risk, shipping 
market supply and demand model. The four shipping markets- freight 
market, sale and purchase market, newbuilding market and demolition 
market.  Classification of costs, Financing ships and shipping companies, 
Risk and returns. 
9

(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks)

SEMESTER S8 
              TRADITIONAL BOAT BUILDING TECHNIQUES 
  
Course Code 
PENST864 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R)

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 
1. Understand the history of traditional boatbuilding.  
2. Discern the methodologies for design and construction of traditional boats 
3. Understand the safety and certification regulations for traditional boatbuilding 
4. Understand launching and post launching activities in modern times 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
History/background. Construction techniques; designers’ plans; building 
moulds, jigs and strong-backs. Wooden kit boats, skills required, different types 
of wood/timber used in boat building. Regional boats of India and other 
countries – Snake boats, house boats, Urus of Malabar, Kerala; Dhows of 
Mandvi, Gujarat; Teppas of Ganjam, Odisha; Boats of Zanzibar, Iran, UK and 
Hong Kong. 
9 
2 
Yard selection, workshop/yard requirements, budgeting and costs, project 
management, outsourcing parts, buy or lease/machinery and tools, bill of 
materials/detailed costs.  
Boats’s outfitting; internal layouts; electrical systems; water and sanitation 
systems; safety equipment and navigation systems; anchoring, mooring and 
deck fittings; painting of the boat PROPN? 
9  
3 
CE Certification, Type Approval/Licensing, Legal Requirements, VAT/ Goods 
Service Tax etc, Warranties/Manuals, Basic Safety at Sea, Skills required & sub- 
contracting, Insurance, Inland Waterway Regulations. 
9  

 
 
4 
Boat relocation, Launching, Ways of lifting & launching a vessel, The actual 
launch, Stepping the mast, Types of berth/moorings, Sea Trials, Modifications 
9
